Chapter 5

Hestia

hestia
Ah, there you are.
Not bad. The camp, I mean.
kyra

hestia

Well, going forward I figure you'll probably find me around here.
I'll see about keeping you folks supplied with basic weaponry at all times.
I know my alchemy, too. Come to me if you need more tomes.

I'll need funding if I'm to make you stuff. Them's the breaks.
kyra

hestia

If you want to know what's for sale just about anywhere,
I'd be happy to give you a preview.
kyra

hestia

I'll let you know if I come up with something special you can use.
kyra

hestia

Now, this is the most important part...
kyra
Yeah?

kyra
Heh. I'll try.

I gave my life to the Mother, and She gleefully took it from me.

......

I try to find purpose in my wretched life, while I still cling on to it.

What manner of deity do you believe in?
fazang
We do not have one deity to worship like you do.
In our eyes, life was not created. It merely is.
Forever circling a core, in an endless cycle.
kairos
And what would that core be?
fazang
It is not a physical entity, as it were. It is a more... abstract concept.
It would be more apt to say the cycle itself drives the core.
All things die, and in so doing, they return to their genesis.
Then the cycle begins anew. A neverending spiral of life.
kairos
(smiles) A beautiful sermon, spoken in perfect Tartaran.
Makes me feel rather inadequate, I'll admit.
fazang
Why don't you give it a try? Explain your faith to me.
kairos
(frowns) I don't know if I'm the right person to do that, honestly.
The church preaches that the Mother is perfect in all things.
That we, Her children, must never question Her design.
Merely look to the heavens, pray and be good little lambs...
I know this is what my answer must be. I know that.
fazang
Do you disagree?
kairos
She is also described as kind, loving and motherly.
I cannot help but detect a major discrepancy there.
I would call my own mother kind, loving and motherly.
But she taught me to follow my path and draw my own conclusions.
To understand those who are different, and forgive they who sin.
How could She hate Her children for such a vague slight as being “heretical?”
fazang
Hmm.
kairos
I do believe the Mother exists, or at least, existed. I am not that far gone.
But... In my opinion, the church stopped giving a fig about Her a long time ago.
They use Her name in vain to subdue the people into absolute compliance.
It... It disgusts me, I won't lie.
fazang
And like the cycle of life, our conversation returns to its root.
You have explained your grievances with the Church of Anima.
Now, I reiterate. Please, explain your faith to me, Kairos.
kairos
......
I believe the Mother asks naught of us, but to be as kind and caring as She is.
That's the man I try to be, and that's what I would ask my brethren to be.
fazang
Is it as simple as that?
kairos
Mmhmm. Told you you were asking the wrong person.
fazang
(smiles) On the contrary. This has been a truly enlightening conversation.
It is always fascinating discussing other doctrines.
Doubly so when it is with a person as wise and pious as you are.
(Kairos laughs.)
kairos
Pffft! You've got to be joking, Fazang.
fazang
(serious) I am not known to tell jokes often.
The Theocracy of Tartaros may fall, but a faith does not so easily fade away.
The Church of Anima, in some capacity or other, will survive.
It was once led astray, but it can yet be brought back to the right path.
Take care, Kairos, for that task will fall upon people such as you.
kairos
(smiles) ...Thanks, Fazang. That's nice to hear.
You take care too, huh?
fazang
May we both see the calm, blue skies after this dreadful storm of war.
